srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_the_Isle_of_Man.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Isle_of_Man.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_the_Isle_of_Man.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_Isle_of_Man.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="300" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a></th><td>\n2,403<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg/23px-Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg/35px-Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg/45px-Flag_of_Hong_Kong.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a><sup><small>G</small></sup></th><td>\n1,459<sup id="cite_ref-The_Stationery_Office_2014_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Stationery_Office_2014-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Carr_2009_13_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carr_2009_13-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#b0c4de;">Languages</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> (<a href="/wiki/Scottish_English" title="Scottish English">Scottish English</a>)<br /> <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Gaelic language">Scottish Gaelic</a><br /> <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#b0c4de;">Religion</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<a href="/wiki/Presbyterianism" title="Presbyterianism">Presbyterianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Episcopal_Church" title="Scottish Episcopal Church">Episcopalianism</a>; other minority groups</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;padding-top:0.5em;font-size:85%;text-align:left;">\n<hr /><sup><small>A</small></sup> These figures are estimates based on census data of populations and official surveys of identity.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (December 2016)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2016)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n<ul><li><sup><small>B</small></sup> <a href="/wiki/Scottish_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish American">Scottish American</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scotch-Irish_Americans" title="Scotch-Irish Americans">Scotch-Irish Americans</a></li>\n<li><sup><small>C</small></sup> <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Canadians" title="Scottish Canadians">Scottish Canadians</a></li>\n<li><sup><small>D</small></sup> Scottish-born people in England only</li>\n<li><sup><small>E</small></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots_people" title="Ulster Scots people">Ulster-Scots</a></li>\n<li><sup><small>G</small></sup> Number of people born in Scotland.</li></ul>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Scottish people</b> (<a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a>: <i>Scots Fowk</i>; <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a>: <i>Albannaich</i>) or <b>Scots</b>, are a <a href="/wiki/Nation" title="Nation">nation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a> native to <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>. Historically, they emerged from an amalgamation of two <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">Celtic</a>-speaking peoples, the <a href="/wiki/Picts" title="Picts">Picts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gaels" title="Gaels">Gaels</a>, who founded the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Kingdom of Scotland</a> (or <i><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Alba" title="Kingdom of Alba">Alba</a></i>) in the 9th century. Later, the neighbouring Celtic-speaking <a href="/wiki/Britons_(historical)" class="mw-redirect" title="Britons (historical)">Cumbrians</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic</a>-speaking <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norse</a>, were incorporated into the Scottish nation.\n</p><p>In modern usage, "Scottish people" or "Scots" is used to refer to anyone whose linguistic, cultural, family ancestral or genetic origins are from Scotland. The <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> word <i><a href="/wiki/Scoti" title="Scoti">Scoti</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> originally referred to the Gaels, but came to describe all inhabitants of Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Considered <a href="/wiki/Archaism" title="Archaism">archaic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Pejorative" title="Pejorative">pejorative</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> the term <b><a href="/wiki/Scotch_(adjective)" title="Scotch (adjective)">Scotch</a></b> has also been used for Scottish people, primarily outside Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Kenneth_Galbraith" title="John Kenneth Galbraith">John Kenneth Galbraith</a> in his book <i>The Scotch</i> (Toronto: MacMillan, 1964) documents the descendants of 19th-century Scottish pioneers who settled in <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_Ontario" title="Southwestern Ontario">Southwestern Ontario</a> and affectionately referred to themselves as \'Scotch\'. He states the book was meant to give a true picture of life in the community in the early decades of the 20th century.\n</p><p>People of Scottish descent live in many countries other than Scotland. Emigration, influenced by factors such as the <a href="/wiki/Highland_Clearances" title="Highland Clearances">Highland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lowland_Clearances" title="Lowland Clearances">Lowland Clearances</a>, Scottish participation in the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>, and latterly <a href="/wiki/Deindustrialization" title="Deindustrialization">industrial decline</a> and unemployment, have resulted in Scottish people being found throughout the world. Scottish emigrants took with them their <a href="/wiki/Scottish_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish languages">Scottish languages</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish culture">culture</a>. Large populations of Scottish people settled the new-world lands of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North</a> and South America, Australia and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>. Canada has the highest level of Scottish descendants per capita in the world and the second-largest population of Scottish descendants, after the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scotland has seen migration and settlement of many peoples at different periods in <a href="/wiki/History_of_Scotland" title="History of Scotland">its history</a>. The Gaels, the Picts and the Britons have their respective origin myths, like most medieval European peoples. <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a> peoples, such as the Anglo-Saxons, arrived beginning in the 7th century, while the Norse settled parts of Scotland from the 8th century onwards. In the <a href="/wiki/Scotland_in_the_High_Middle_Ages" title="Scotland in the High Middle Ages">High Middle Ages</a>, from the reign of <a href="/wiki/David_I_of_Scotland" title="David I of Scotland">David I of Scotland</a>, there was some emigration from France, England and the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a> to Scotland. Some famous Scottish family names, including those bearing the names which became <a href="/wiki/Bruce" title="Bruce">Bruce</a>, <a href="/wiki/House_of_Balliol" title="House of Balliol">Balliol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murray_(surname)" title="Murray (surname)">Murray</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stewart_(name)" title="Stewart (name)">Stewart</a> came to Scotland at this time. Today Scotland is <a href="/wiki/Countries_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Countries of the United Kingdom">one of the countries</a> of the United Kingdom, and the majority of people living there are <a href="/wiki/British_nationality_law" title="British nationality law">British citizens</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" Scotland</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Scottish_diaspora"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Scottish diaspora</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Language"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Language</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-18"><a class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Folklore"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">Folklore</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a class="toctext">Etymology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#Sources"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Sources</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups_of_Scotland">Ethnic groups of Scotland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups of Scotland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Genetic_history_of_the_British_Isles" title="Genetic history of the British Isles">Genetic history of the British Isles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Scotland" title="Prehistoric Scotland">Prehistoric Scotland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Scotland" title="Scandinavian Scotland">Scandinavian Scotland</a></div>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Early_Middle_Ages" title="Early Middle Ages">Early Middle Ages</a>, Scotland saw several ethnic or cultural groups mentioned in contemporary sources, namely the <a href="/wiki/Picts" title="Picts">Picts</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gaels" title="Gaels">Gaels</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brythons" class="mw-redirect" title="Brythons">Britons</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Angles" title="Angles">Angles</a>, with the latter settling in the southeast of the country. Culturally, these peoples are grouped according to language. Most of Scotland until the 13th century spoke <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">Celtic languages</a> and these included, at least initially, the <a href="/wiki/Brythons" class="mw-redirect" title="Brythons">Britons</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Gaels" title="Gaels">Gaels</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Picts" title="Picts">Picts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic peoples</a> included the Angles of <a href="/wiki/Northumbria" class="mw-redirect" title="Northumbria">Northumbria</a>, who settled in south-eastern Scotland in the region between the <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Forth" title="Firth of Forth">Firth of Forth</a> to the north and the <a href="/wiki/River_Tweed" title="River Tweed">River Tweed</a> to the south. They also occupied the south-west of Scotland up to and including the Plain of <a href="/wiki/Kyle,_Ayrshire" title="Kyle, Ayrshire">Kyle</a> and their language, <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a>, was the earliest form of the language which eventually became known as <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a>.\n</p><p>Use of the Gaelic language spread throughout nearly the whole of Scotland by the 9th century,<sup id="cite_ref-bord-na-gaidhlig1_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bord-na-gaidhlig1-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> reaching a peak in the 11th to 13th centuries, but was never the language of the south-east of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-bord-na-gaidhlig1_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bord-na-gaidhlig1-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edgar_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Edgar of England">King Edgar</a> \ndivided the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Northumbria" title="Kingdom of Northumbria">Kingdom of Northumbria</a> between Scotland and England; at least, most medieval historians now accept the \'gift\' by Edgar, in any case, after the later <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Carham" title="Battle of Carham">Battle of Carham</a> the Scottish kingdom encompassed many English people, with even more quite possibly arriving after the <a href="/wiki/Norman_invasion_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman invasion of England">Norman invasion of England</a> in 1066. South-east of the <a href="/wiki/Firth_of_Forth" title="Firth of Forth">Firth of Forth</a>, then in <a href="/wiki/Lothian" title="Lothian">Lothian</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Borders" title="Scottish Borders">Borders</a> (<a href="/wiki/Old_English_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Old English language">OE:</a> <i>Lo\xc3\xb0ene</i>), a northern variety of <a href="/wiki/Old_English_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Old English language">Old English</a>, also known as <a href="/wiki/Early_Scots" title="Early Scots">Early Scots</a>, was spoken.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St-Kildans.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/St-Kildans.jpg/220px-St-Kildans.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/St-Kildans.jpg/330px-St-Kildans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/St-Kildans.jpg/440px-St-Kildans.jpg 2x" data-file-width="899" data-file-height="581" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St-Kildans.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St_Kilda,_Scotland" title="St Kilda, Scotland">St. Kildans</a> sitting on the village street, 1886</div></div></div>\n<p>As a result of <a href="/wiki/David_I_of_Scotland" title="David I of Scotland">David I, King of Scots\'</a> return from exile in England in 1113, ultimately to assume the throne in 1124 with the help of <a href="/wiki/Normans" title="Normans">Norman</a> military force, David invited Norman families from France and England to settle in lands he granted them to spread a ruling class loyal to him.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>  This <a href="/wiki/Davidian_Revolution" title="Davidian Revolution">Davidian Revolution</a>, as many historians call it, brought a European style of <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudalism</a> to Scotland along with an influx of people of Norman descent - by invitation, unlike <a href="/wiki/Norman_conquest_of_England" title="Norman conquest of England">England</a> where it was by conquest. To this day, many of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_surnames" title="Scottish surnames">common family names of Scotland</a> can trace ancestry to Normans from this period, such as the <a href="/wiki/Stewart_(name)" title="Stewart (name)">Stewarts</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bruce" title="Bruce">Bruces</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_(surname_and_title)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamilton (surname and title)">Hamiltons</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Clan_Wallace#Origins_of_the_clan" title="Clan Wallace">Wallaces</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Melville_(name)" title="Melville (name)">Melvilles</a>, some <a href="/wiki/Clan_Broun" title="Clan Broun">Browns</a> and many others.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Northern_Isles" title="Northern Isles">Northern Isles</a> and some parts of <a href="/wiki/Caithness" title="Caithness">Caithness</a> were <a href="/wiki/Norn_language" title="Norn language">Norn</a>-speaking (the west of Caithness was Gaelic-speaking into the 20th century, as were some small communities in parts of the Central Highlands). From 1200 to 1500 the <a href="/wiki/Early_Scots" title="Early Scots">Early Scots</a> language spread across the lowland parts of Scotland between <a href="/wiki/Galloway" title="Galloway">Galloway</a> and the Highland line, being used by <a href="/wiki/John_Barbour_(poet)" title="John Barbour (poet)">Barbour</a> in his historical epic <i><a href="/wiki/The_Brus" title="The Brus">The Brus</a></i> in the late 14th century in Aberdeen.\n</p><p>From 1500 on, Scotland was commonly divided by language into two groups of people, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Gaelic language">Gaelic-speaking</a> "<a href="/wiki/Scottish_Highlands" title="Scottish Highlands">Highlanders</a>" (the language formerly called Scottis by English speakers and known by many Lowlanders in the 18th century as "Irish") and the <a href="/wiki/Early_Scots" title="Early Scots">Inglis</a>-speaking "<a href="/wiki/Scottish_Lowlands" title="Scottish Lowlands">Lowlanders</a>" (a language later to be called <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a>). Today, immigrants have brought other languages, but almost every adult throughout Scotland is fluent in the English language.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scottish_diaspora">Scottish diaspora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Scottish diaspora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_diaspora" title="Scottish diaspora">Scottish diaspora</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots_people" title="Ulster Scots people">Ulster Scots people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Highland_Clearances" title="Highland Clearances">Highland Clearances</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lowland_Clearances" title="Lowland Clearances">Lowland Clearances</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="float:right;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="4">Number of the Scottish diaspora\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Census Year\n</th>\n<th>Population\n</th>\n<th colspan="4">% of the local population\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left; text-indent:30px;"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia"><img alt="Australia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="640" /></a></span> 2011 <a href="/wiki/Census_in_Australia" title="Census in Australia">Australia</a><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td>1,792,622\n</td>\n<td align="right"><b>8.3</b>\n</td>\n<td align="left"><span style="display:none;">8.3</span><div style="width:16.6px;height:2ex;background:#aaa;background:darkblue">&#160;</div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left; text-indent:30px;"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" /></a></span> 2010 <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census" title="United States Census">United States</a> <a href="/wiki/American_Community_Survey" title="American Community Survey">ACS</a><sup id="cite_ref-United_States_Census_Bureau_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_States_Census_Bureau-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td>5,460,679\n</td>\n<td align="right"><b>1.5</b>\n</td>\n<td align="left"><span style="display:none;">1.5</span><div style="width:3px;height:2ex;background:#aaa;background:darkblue">&#160;</div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left; text-indent:30px;"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" /></a></span> 2010 U.S (Scotch-Irish)<sup id="cite_ref-United_States_Census_Bureau_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_States_Census_Bureau-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td>3,257,161\n</td>\n<td align="right"><b>1.1</b>\n</td>\n<td align="left"><span style="display:none;">1.1</span><div style="width:2.2px;height:2ex;background:#aaa;background:darkblue">&#160;</div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left; text-indent:30px;"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada"><img alt="Canada" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/23px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/35px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Flag_of_Canada.svg/46px-Flag_of_Canada.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="500" /></a></span> 2011 <a href="/wiki/Canada_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="Canada Census">Canada</a><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td>4,714,965\n</td>\n<td align="right"><b>14.35</b>\n</td>\n<td align="left"><span style="display:none;">14.35</span><div style="width:28.7px;height:2ex;background:#aaa;background:darkblue">&#160;</div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Today, Scotland has a population of just over five million people,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>  the majority of whom consider themselves Scottish.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In addition, there are many more people with Scots ancestry living abroad than the total population of Scotland.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Americans" title="Scottish Americans">Scottish Americans</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Andrew_Carnegie,_three-quarter_length_portrait,_seated,_facing_slightly_left,_1913.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Andrew_Carnegie%2C_three-quarter_length_portrait%2C_seated%2C_facing_slightly_left%2C_1913.jpg/170px-Andrew_Carnegie%2C_three-quarter_length_portrait%2C_seated%2C_facing_slightly_left%2C_1913.jpg" width="170" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Andrew_Carnegie%2C_three-quarter_length_portrait%2C_seated%2C_facing_slightly_left%2C_1913.jpg/255px-Andrew_Carnegie%2C_three-quarter_length_portrait%2C_seated%2C_facing_slightly_left%2C_1913.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Andrew_Carnegie%2C_three-quarter_length_portrait%2C_seated%2C_facing_slightly_left%2C_1913.jpg/340px-Andrew_Carnegie%2C_three-quarter_length_portrait%2C_seated%2C_facing_slightly_left%2C_1913.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2574" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Andrew_Carnegie,_three-quarter_length_portrait,_seated,_facing_slightly_left,_1913.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scottish-born American industrialist and philanthropist <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie" title="Andrew Carnegie">Andrew Carnegie</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In the 2013 <a href="/wiki/American_Community_Survey" title="American Community Survey">American Community Survey</a> 5,310,285 identified as Scottish and 2,976,878 as of Scots-Irish descent.<sup id="cite_ref-United_States_Census_Bureau_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_States_Census_Bureau-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Americans" title="Americans">Americans</a> of Scottish descent outnumber the population of Scotland, where 4,459,071 or 88.09% of people identified as ethnic Scottish in the 2001 Census.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_y_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_y-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ref_b_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_b-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The number of Americans of Scottish descent today is estimated to be 20 to 25 million<sup id="cite_ref-McCarthy_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCarthy-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Scotlandnow_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotlandnow-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SPOR_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SPOR-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SPEERCA_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SPEERCA-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> (up to 8.3% of the total US population), and Scotch-Irish, 27 to 30 million<sup id="cite_ref-Webb2004_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Webb2004-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Secret_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Secret-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> (up to 10% of the total US population),<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> the subgroups overlapping and not always distinguishable because of their shared ancestral <a href="/wiki/Surname" title="Surname">surnames</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\nThe majority of Scotch-Irish originally came from Lowland Scotland and Northern England<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> before migrating to the province of <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> in <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> (see <i><a href="/wiki/Plantation_of_Ulster" title="Plantation of Ulster">Plantation of Ulster</a></i>)  and thence, beginning about five <a href="/wiki/Generation" title="Generation">generations</a> later, to North America in large numbers during the eighteenth century.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Canadians" title="Scottish Canadians">Scottish Canadians</a></div>\n<p>As the third-largest <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a> in Canada and amongst the first Europeans to settle in the country, Scottish people have made a large impact on <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Canada" title="Culture of Canada">Canadian culture</a> since colonial times. According to the <a href="/wiki/Canada_2011_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="Canada 2011 Census">2011 Census of Canada</a>, the number of Canadians claiming full or partial Scottish descent is 4,714,970,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> or 15.10% of the nation\'s total population.\n</p><p>Many respondents may have misunderstood the question and the numerous responses for "Canadian" does not give an accurate figure for numerous groups, particularly those of British Isles origins. Scottish-Canadians are the 3rd biggest ethnic group in Canada. Scottish culture has particularly thrived in the Canadian province of <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> for "New Scotland"). There, in <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Regional_Municipality,_Nova_Scotia" class="mw-redirect" title="Cape Breton Regional Municipality, Nova Scotia">Cape Breton</a>, where both lowland and highland Scots settled in large numbers, <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Gaelic" title="Canadian Gaelic">Canadian Gaelic</a> is still spoken by a small number of residents. Cape Breton is the home of the <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_College_of_Celtic_Arts_and_Crafts" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaelic College of Celtic Arts and Crafts">Gaelic College of Celtic Arts and Crafts</a>. <a href="/wiki/Glengarry_County,_Ontario" title="Glengarry County, Ontario">Glengarry County</a> in present-day <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Ontario" title="Eastern Ontario">Eastern Ontario</a> is a historic county that was set up as a settlement for <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Highlands" title="Scottish Highlands">Highland Scots</a>, where many from the Highlands settled to preserve their culture in result of the Highland Clearances. Gaelic was the native language of the community since its settlement in the 18th century although the number of speakers decreased since as a result of English migration<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. As of the modern 21st century, there are still a few Gaelic speakers in the community.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Australians" title="Scottish Australians">Scottish Australians</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomasbrisbane.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Thomasbrisbane.jpg/170px-Thomasbrisbane.jpg" width="170" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Thomasbrisbane.jpg/255px-Thomasbrisbane.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fe/Thomasbrisbane.jpg 2x" data-file-width="268" data-file-height="350" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomasbrisbane.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Australian city of <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a> is named after Scotsman <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Brisbane" title="Thomas Brisbane">Thomas Brisbane</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>By 1830, 15.11% of the colonies\' total population were Scots, which increased by the middle of the century to 25,000, or 20-25% of the total population. The <a href="/wiki/Australian_Gold_Rush" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Gold Rush">Australian Gold Rush</a> of the 1850s provided a further impetus for Scottish migration: in the 1850s 90,000 Scots immigrated to Australia, far more than other British or Irish populations at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Australian_People_2001_p650_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Australian_People_2001_p650-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Literacy rates of the Scottish immigrants ran at 90-95%. By 1860, Scots made up 50% of the ethnic composition of <a href="/wiki/Western_Victoria" title="Western Victoria">Western Victoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Penola,_South_Australia" title="Penola, South Australia">Penola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Naracoorte,_South_Australia" title="Naracoorte, South Australia">Naracoorte</a>. Other settlements in <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a> included <a href="/wiki/New_England_(Australia)" class="mw-redirect" title="New England (Australia)">New England</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hunter_Region" title="Hunter Region">Hunter Valley</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Illawarra" title="Illawarra">Illawarra</a>.\n</p><p>Much settlement followed the <a href="/wiki/Highland_Potato_Famine" title="Highland Potato Famine">Highland Potato Famine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Highland_Clearances" title="Highland Clearances">Highland Clearances</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lowland_Clearances" title="Lowland Clearances">Lowland Clearances</a> of the mid-19th century.\nIn the 1840s, Scots-born immigrants constituted 12% of the Australian population. Out of the 1.3 million migrants from Britain to Australia in the period from 1861\xe2\x80\x931914, 13.5% were Scots. Just 5.3% of the convicts transported to Eastern Australia between 1789 and 1852 were Scots.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A steady rate of Scottish immigration continued into the 20th century and substantial numbers of Scots continued to arrive after 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-Australia_2008_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Australia_2008-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> From 1900 until the 1950s, Scots favoured New South Wales, as well as Western Australia and Southern Australia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> A strong cultural Scottish presence is evident in the <a href="/wiki/Highland_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="Highland Games">Highland Games</a>, dance, <a href="/wiki/Tartan_Day" title="Tartan Day">Tartan Day</a> celebrations, clan and Gaelic-speaking societies found throughout modern Australia.\n</p><p>According to the 2011 Australian census, 130,204 Australian residents were born in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ABS_Country_of_Birth_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABS_Country_of_Birth-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> while 1,792,600 claimed Scottish ancestry, either alone or in combination with another ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-abs.gov.au_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abs.gov.au-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> This is the fourth most commonly nominated ancestry and represents over 8.9% of the total population of Australia.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_New_Zealanders" title="Scottish New Zealanders">Scottish New Zealanders</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Allsworth_-_The_emigrants_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/William_Allsworth_-_The_emigrants_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/220px-William_Allsworth_-_The_emigrants_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/William_Allsworth_-_The_emigrants_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/330px-William_Allsworth_-_The_emigrants_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/William_Allsworth_-_The_emigrants_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/440px-William_Allsworth_-_The_emigrants_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8323" data-file-height="6115" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Allsworth_-_The_emigrants_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scottish Highland family migrating to <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> in 1844</div></div></div>\n<p>Significant numbers of Scottish people also settled in New Zealand. Approximately 20 percent of the original European settler population of New Zealand came from Scotland, and Scottish influence is still visible around the country.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/South_Island" title="South Island">South Island</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Dunedin" title="Dunedin">Dunedin</a>, in particular, is known for its Scottish heritage and was named as a tribute to <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> by the city\'s Scottish founders.\n</p><p>Scottish migration to New Zealand dates back to the earliest period of European colonisation, with a large proportion of <a href="/wiki/P%C4%81keh%C4%81" title="P\xc4\x81keh\xc4\x81">P\xc4\x81keh\xc4\x81</a> New Zealanders being of Scottish descent.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> However, identification as "British" or "European" New Zealanders can sometimes obscure their origin. Many Scottish New Zealanders also have <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_people" title="M\xc4\x81ori people">M\xc4\x81ori</a> or other non-European ancestry.\n</p><p>The majority of Scottish immigrants settled in the South Island. All over New Zealand, the Scots developed different means to bridge the old homeland and the new. Many <a href="/wiki/Caledonia" title="Caledonia">Caledonian</a> societies were formed, well over 100 by the early twentieth century, who helped maintain Scottish culture and traditions. From the 1860s, these societies organised annual Caledonian Games throughout New Zealand. The Games were sports meets that brought together Scottish settlers and the wider New Zealand public. In so doing, the Games gave Scots a path to cultural integration as Scottish New Zealanders.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In the 1961 <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_census" title="New Zealand census">census</a> there were 47,078 people living in New Zealand who were born in Scotland; in the <a href="/wiki/2013_New_Zealand_census" title="2013 New Zealand census">2013 census</a> there were 25,953 in this category.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:268px;max-width:268px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:132px;max-width:132px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Carol_Ann_Duffy_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Carol_Ann_Duffy_%28cropped%29.jpg/130px-Carol_Ann_Duffy_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="130" height="168" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Carol_Ann_Duffy_%28cropped%29.jpg/195px-Carol_Ann_Duffy_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Carol_Ann_Duffy_%28cropped%29.jpg/260px-Carol_Ann_Duffy_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="564" data-file-height="730" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Carol_Ann_Duffy" title="Carol Ann Duffy">Carol Ann Duffy</a>, the first woman and the first Scottish person to be appointed the <a href="/wiki/Poet_Laureate_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Poet Laureate of the United Kingdom">Poet Laureate of the United Kingdom</a><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:132px;max-width:132px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Jackie_Kay3.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Jackie_Kay3.JPG/130px-Jackie_Kay3.JPG" width="130" height="173" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Jackie_Kay3.JPG/195px-Jackie_Kay3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Jackie_Kay3.JPG/260px-Jackie_Kay3.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1600" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Jackie_Kay" title="Jackie Kay">Jackie Kay</a>, Scotland\'s <a href="/wiki/Makar" title="Makar">makar</a>, or national poet<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>Many people of Scottish descent live in other parts of the United Kingdom. In <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a> particularly the colonial policies of <a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">James VI</a>, known as the <a href="/wiki/Plantation_of_Ulster" title="Plantation of Ulster">plantation of Ulster</a>, resulted in a Presbyterian and Scottish society, which formed the <a href="/wiki/Ulster-Scots" class="mw-redirect" title="Ulster-Scots">Ulster-Scots</a> community.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Ascendancy" title="Protestant Ascendancy">Protestant Ascendancy</a> did not however benefit them much, as the English espoused the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican Church">Anglican Church</a>. The number of people of Scottish descent in England and Wales is difficult to quantify due to the many complex migrations on the island,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and ancient migration patterns due to wars, famine and conquest.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The 2011 Census recorded 708,872 people born in Scotland resident in England, 24,346 resident in Wales<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and 15,455 resident in Northern Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2016)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> \n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rest_of_Europe">Rest of Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Rest of Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Other European countries have had their share of Scots immigrants. The Scots have emigrated to mainland Europe for centuries as merchants and soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Many emigrated to France, Poland,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Italian-Scots" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian-Scots">Italy</a>, Germany, Scandinavia,<sup id="cite_ref-diaspora_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diaspora-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> and the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Recently some scholars suggested that up to 250,000 Russian nationals may have Scottish ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guy_Scott.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Guy_Scott.png/140px-Guy_Scott.png" width="140" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Guy_Scott.png/210px-Guy_Scott.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Guy_Scott.png/280px-Guy_Scott.png 2x" data-file-width="460" data-file-height="566" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guy_Scott.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Guy_Scott" title="Guy Scott">Guy Scott</a>, the 12th vice-president and acting president of <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> from Oct 2014 \xe2\x80\x93 Jan 2015, is of Scottish descent.</div></div></div>\n<p>A number of Scottish people settled in South Africa in the 1800s and were known for their road-building expertise, their farming experience, and architectural skills.<sup id="cite_ref-ZAscotland_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZAscotland-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_America">Latin America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Latin America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The largest population of Scots in Latin America is found in <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2016)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> followed by <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2016)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scots_in_mainland_Europe">Scots in mainland Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Scots in mainland Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>It is said<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (September 2013)">by whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> that the first people from the <a href="/wiki/Low_Countries" title="Low Countries">Low Countries</a> to settle in Scotland came in the wake of <a href="/wiki/Maud,_Countess_of_Huntingdon" title="Maud, Countess of Huntingdon">Maud\'s</a> marriage to the Scottish king, <a href="/wiki/David_I_of_Scotland" title="David I of Scotland">David I</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/Scotland_in_the_High_Middle_Ages" title="Scotland in the High Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (December 2016)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Craftsmen and tradesmen followed courtiers and in later centuries a brisk trade grew up between the two nations: Scotland\'s primary goods (wool, hides, salmon and then coal) in exchange for the luxuries obtainable in the Netherlands, one of the major hubs of European trade.\n</p><p>By 1600, trading colonies had grown up on either side of the well-travelled shipping routes: the Dutch settled along the eastern seaboard of Scotland; the Scots congregating first in <a href="/wiki/Campvere" class="mw-redirect" title="Campvere">Campvere</a>\xe2\x80\x94where they were allowed to land their goods duty-free and run their own affairs\xe2\x80\x94and then in <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>, where Scottish and Dutch <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a> coexisted comfortably. Besides the thousands (or, according to one estimate, over 1 million)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> of local descendants with Scots ancestry, both ports still show signs of these early alliances. Now a museum, \'The Scots House\' in the town of <a href="/wiki/Veere" title="Veere">Veere</a> was the only place outwith Scotland where <a href="/wiki/Scots_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Scots Law">Scots Law</a> was practised. In Rotterdam, meanwhile, the doors of the <a href="/wiki/Scots_International_Church" title="Scots International Church">Scots International Church</a> have remained open since 1643.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Russians" title="Scottish Russians">Scottish Russians</a></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FotoGordon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/FotoGordon.jpg/150px-FotoGordon.jpg" width="150" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/FotoGordon.jpg/225px-FotoGordon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/53/FotoGordon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="255" data-file-height="312" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FotoGordon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Patrick_Gordon" title="Patrick Gordon">Patrick Gordon</a> was a Russian General originally from Scotland and a friend of <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The first Scots to be mentioned in Russia\'s history were the Scottish soldiers in <a href="/wiki/Muscovy" class="mw-redirect" title="Muscovy">Muscovy</a> referred to as early as in the 14th century.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Among the \'soldiers of fortune\' was the ancestor to famous Russian poet <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lermontov" title="Mikhail Lermontov">Mikhail Lermontov</a>, called George Learmonth. A number of Scots gained wealth and fame in the times of <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine the Great</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> These include <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Gordon" title="Patrick Gordon">Patrick Gordon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Menzies" class="mw-redirect" title="Paul Menzies">Paul Menzies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Greig" title="Samuel Greig">Samuel Greig</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Baird_(engineer)" title="Charles Baird (engineer)">Charles Baird</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Cameron_(architect)" title="Charles Cameron (architect)">Charles Cameron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adam_Menelaws" title="Adam Menelaws">Adam Menelaws</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Heste" title="William Heste">William Hastie</a>. Several doctors to the Russian court were from Scotland,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> the best known being <a href="/wiki/Sir_James_Wylie,_1st_Baronet" title="Sir James Wylie, 1st Baronet">James Wylie</a>.\n</p><p>The next wave of migration established commercial links with Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 19th century witnessed the immense literary cross-references between Scotland and Russia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2012)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>A Russian scholar, Maria Koroleva, distinguishes between \'the Russian Scots\' (properly assimilated) and \'Scots in Russia\', who remained thoroughly Scottish.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are several societies in contemporary Russia to unite<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2012)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> the Scots. The Russian census lists does not distinguish Scots from other British people, so it is hard to establish reliable figures for the number of Scots living and working in modern Russia.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poland">Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>From as far back as the mid-16th century there were Scots trading and settling in <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> A "Scotch Pedlar\'s Pack in Poland" became a proverbial expression. It usually consisted of cloths, woollen goods and linen kerchiefs (head coverings). Itinerants also sold tin utensils and ironware such as scissors and knives. Along with the protection offered by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_B%C3%A1thory" title="Stephen B\xc3\xa1thory">King Stephen</a> in the Royal Grant of 1576, a district in <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Krak\xc3\xb3w">Krak\xc3\xb3w</a> was assigned to Scottish immigrants.\n</p><p>Records from 1592 mention Scots settlers granted citizenship of Krak\xc3\xb3w, and give their employment as trader or merchant. Fees for citizenship ranged from 12 Polish florins to a musket and gunpowder, or an undertaking to marry within a year and a day of acquiring a holding.\n</p><p>By the 17th century, an estimated 30,000 to 40,000 Scots lived in the <a href="/wiki/Polish-Lithuanian_Commonwealth" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish-Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish-Lithuanian Commonwealth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-diaspora_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diaspora-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Many came from <a href="/wiki/Dundee" title="Dundee">Dundee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Scots could be found in Polish towns on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Vistula" title="Vistula">Vistula</a> as far south as <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Krak\xc3\xb3w">Krak\xc3\xb3w</a>. Settlers from <a href="/wiki/Aberdeenshire" title="Aberdeenshire">Aberdeenshire</a> were mainly Episcopalians or Catholics, but there were also large numbers of Calvinists. As well as Scottish traders, there were also many Scottish soldiers in Poland. In 1656, a number of Scottish highlanders who were disenchanted with <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a>\'s rule went to Poland to join the service of the <a href="/wiki/Charles_X_Gustav_of_Sweden" title="Charles X Gustav of Sweden">King of Sweden</a> in his <a href="/wiki/Deluge_(history)#Swedish_invasion" title="Deluge (history)">war against it</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Murray_(admiral)" title="James Murray (admiral)">James Murray</a> created the Polish navy <sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (October 2018)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and participated in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Oliwa" title="Battle of Oliwa">Battle of Oliwa</a>. A series of four Polish novels include him as <i>Captain Mora</i> or <i>Flying Scotsman</i>. The writer Jerzy Bogdan Rychli\xc5\x84ski was supported by navy historian Jerzy Pertek. <sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Scots integrated well and many acquired great wealth. They contributed to many charitable institutions in the host country, but did not forget their homeland; for example, in 1701 when collections were made for the restoration fund of the <a href="/wiki/Marischal_College" title="Marischal College">Marischal College</a>, Aberdeen, Scottish settlers in Poland gave generously.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Many royal grants and privileges were granted to Scottish merchants until the 18th century, at which time the settlers began to merge more and more into the native population. <a href="/wiki/Charles_Edward_Stuart" title="Charles Edward Stuart">"Bonnie Prince Charlie"</a> was half Polish, since he was the son of <a href="/wiki/James_Francis_Edward_Stuart" title="James Francis Edward Stuart">James Stuart</a>, the "Old Pretender", and <a href="/wiki/Maria_Clementina_Sobieska" title="Maria Clementina Sobieska">Clementina Sobieska</a>, granddaughter of <a href="/wiki/John_III_Sobieski" title="John III Sobieski">Jan Sobieski</a>, King of Poland.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2016)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2016)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In 1691, the City of <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a> elected the Scottish immigrant <a href="/wiki/Aleksander_Czamer" class="mw-redirect" title="Aleksander Czamer">Aleksander Czamer</a> (Alexander Chalmers) as its mayor.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Novelist <a href="/wiki/Henryk_Sienkiewicz" title="Henryk Sienkiewicz">Henryk Sienkiewicz</a> created a fictitious character, <a href="/wiki/Hassling-Ketling_of_Elgin" title="Hassling-Ketling of Elgin">Hassling-Ketling of Elgin</a>, played by <a href="/wiki/Jan_Nowicki" title="Jan Nowicki">Jan Nowicki</a> in the film <a href="/wiki/Colonel_Wolodyjowski_(film)" title="Colonel Wolodyjowski (film)">Colonel Wolodyjowski</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Italian_Scots" title="Italian Scots">Italian Scots</a></div>\n<p>By 1592, the Scottish community in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> was big enough to merit the building of <a href="/wiki/Sant%27Andrea_degli_Scozzesi" title="Sant&#39;Andrea degli Scozzesi">Sant\'Andrea degli Scozzesi</a> (St Andrew of the Scots). It was constructed for the Scottish expatriate community in Rome, especially for those intended for priesthood. The adjoining hospice was a shelter for Catholic Scots who fled their country because of religious persecution. In 1615, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_V" title="Pope Paul V">Pope Paul V</a> gave the hospice and the nearby Scottish Seminar to the <a href="/wiki/Jesuits" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesuits">Jesuits</a>. It was rebuilt in 1645. The church and facilities became more important when <a href="/wiki/James_Francis_Edward_Stuart" title="James Francis Edward Stuart">James Francis Edward Stuart</a>, the Old Pretender, set up residence in Rome in 1717, but were abandoned during the French occupation of Rome in the late 18th century. In 1820, although religious activity was resumed, it was no longer led by the Jesuits. <a href="/wiki/Sant%27Andrea_degli_Scozzesi" title="Sant&#39;Andrea degli Scozzesi">Sant\'Andrea degli Scozzesi</a> was reconstructed in 1869 by <a href="/wiki/Luigi_Poletti_(architect)" title="Luigi Poletti (architect)">Luigi Poletti</a>. The church was deconsecrated in 1962 and incorporated into a bank (Cassa di Risparmio delle Province Lombarde). The Scottish Seminar also moved away. The <a href="/wiki/St._Andrew%27s_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Andrew&#39;s Day">Feast of St Andrew</a> is still celebrated there on 30 November.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Gurro" title="Gurro">Gurro</a> in Italy is said to be populated by the descendants of Scottish soldiers. According to local legend, Scottish soldiers fleeing the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pavia" title="Battle of Pavia">Battle of Pavia</a> who arrived in the area were stopped by severe blizzards that forced many, if not all, to give up their travels and settle in the town. To this day, the town of Gurro is still proud of its Scottish links. Many of the residents claim that their surnames are Italian translations of Scottish surnames.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The town also has a Scottish museum.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2016)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Scotland" title="Culture of Scotland">Culture of Scotland</a></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:154px;max-width:154px"><div 2x" data-file-width="442" data-file-height="566" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a> and <a \xe2\x80\x93 throughout the <a href="/wiki/Highlands_and_Islands" title="Highlands and Islands">Highlands and Islands of Scotland</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" href="#cite_note-Flockhart-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> and "Scotland\'s Greatest Living National Treasure".<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Watt_James_von_Breda.jpg"
