style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/James_Watt" title="James Watt">James Watt</a>, a Scottish mechanical engineer whose improvements in steam engine technology drove the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>.</div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Language_in_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Language in Scotland">Language in Scotland</a></div>\n<p>Historically, Scottish people have spoken many different languages and dialects. The Pictish language, Norse, Norman-French and Brythonic languages have been spoken by forebears of Scottish people. However, none of these are in use today. The remaining three major languages of the Scottish people are English, <a href="/wiki/Scots_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Scots Language">Scots</a> (various dialects) and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Gaelic</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. Of these three, English is the most common form as a first language. There are some other minority languages of the Scottish people, such as Spanish, used by the population of Scots in <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Norn_language" title="Norn language">Norn language</a> was spoken in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Isles" title="Northern Isles">Northern Isles</a> into the early modern period \xe2\x80\x93 the current dialects of <a href="/wiki/Shetlandic" class="mw-redirect" title="Shetlandic">Shetlandic</a> and Orcadian are heavily influenced by it, to this day.\n</p><p>There is still debate whether Scots is a dialect or a language in its own right, as there is no clear line to define the two. Scots is usually regarded as a midway between the two, as it is highly mutually intelligible with English, particularly the dialects spoken in the North of England as well as those spoken in Scotland, but is treated as a language in some laws.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Scottish_English">Scottish English</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Scottish English">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_English" title="Scottish English">Scottish English</a></div>\n<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Crowns" class="mw-redirect" title="Union of Crowns">Union of Crowns</a> in 1603, the Scottish Court moved with <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="James I of England">James VI &amp; I</a> to London and English vocabulary began to be used by the Scottish upper classes.<sup id="cite_ref-Crystal_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crystal-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> With the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Printing_press" title="Printing press">printing press</a>, spellings became standardised. <a href="/wiki/Scottish_English" title="Scottish English">Scottish English</a>, a Scottish variation of southern <a href="/wiki/English_English" class="mw-redirect" title="English English">English English</a>, began to replace the Scots language. Scottish English soon became the dominant language. By the end of the 17th century, Scots had practically ceased to exist, at least in literary form.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> While Scots remained a common spoken language, the southern Scottish English dialect was the preferred language for publications from the 18th century to the present day. Today most Scottish people speak Scottish English, which has some distinctive vocabulary and may be influenced to varying degrees by Scots.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Scots">Scots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Scots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots language</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots_dialects" title="Ulster Scots dialects">Ulster Scots dialects</a></div>\n<p>Lowland Scots, also known as <a href="/wiki/Lallans" title="Lallans">Lallans</a> or <a href="/wiki/Doric_dialect_(Scotland)" title="Doric dialect (Scotland)">Doric</a>, is a language of <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a> origin. It has its roots in Northern <a href="/wiki/Middle_English" title="Middle English">Middle English</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_Scottish_Independence" title="Wars of Scottish Independence">wars of independence</a>, the English used by Lowland Scots speakers evolved in a different direction from that of Modern <a href="/wiki/English_language_in_England" title="English language in England">English</a>. Since 1424, this language, known to its speakers as <i>Inglis</i>, was used by the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> in its statutes.<sup id="cite_ref-Crystal_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crystal-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> By the middle of the 15th century, the language\'s name had changed from <i>Inglis</i> to <i>Scottis</i>. The <a href="/wiki/Scottish_reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish reformation">reformation</a>, from 1560 onwards, saw the beginning of a decline in the use of Scots forms. With the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterian">Presbyterian</a> religion, and lacking a Scots translation of the Bible, they used the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Edition" class="mw-redirect" title="Geneva Edition">Geneva Edition</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> From that point on, God spoke English, not Scots.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Scots continued to be used in official legal and court documents throughout the 18th century. However, due to the adoption of the southern standard by officialdom and the Education system the use of written Scots declined. Lowland Scots is still a popular spoken language with over 1.5 million Scots speakers in Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Scots is used by about 30,000 <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots_people" title="Ulster Scots people">Ulster Scots</a><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> and is known in official circles as <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Ulster Scots language">Ullans</a>. In 1993, Ulster Scots was recognised, along with Scots, as a variety of the Scots language by the <a href="/wiki/European_Bureau_for_Lesser-Used_Languages" title="European Bureau for Lesser-Used Languages">European Bureau for Lesser-Used Languages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NeuheiserWolff2004_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NeuheiserWolff2004-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Scottish_Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Scottish Gaelic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Gaelic" title="Canadian Gaelic">Canadian Gaelic</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">Celtic language</a> with similarities to Irish. <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a> comes from <a href="/wiki/Old_Irish" title="Old Irish">Old Irish</a>. It was originally spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Gaels" title="Gaels">Gaels</a> of <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1l_Riata" title="D\xc3\xa1l Riata">D\xc3\xa1l Riata</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Rhinns_of_Galloway" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhinns of Galloway">Rhinns of Galloway</a>, later being adopted by the <a href="/wiki/Pictish" class="mw-redirect" title="Pictish">Pictish</a> people of central and eastern Scotland. Gaelic (<i>lingua Scottica</i>, <i>Scottis</i>) became the <i>de facto</i> language of the whole <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Alba" title="Kingdom of Alba">Kingdom of Alba</a>, giving its name to the country (<i>Scotia</i>, "Scotland"). Meanwhile, Gaelic independently spread from <a href="/wiki/Galloway" title="Galloway">Galloway</a> into <a href="/wiki/Dumfriesshire" title="Dumfriesshire">Dumfriesshire</a>. It is unclear if the Gaelic of 12th-century <a href="/wiki/Clydesdale" title="Clydesdale">Clydesdale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Selkirkshire" title="Selkirkshire">Selkirkshire</a> came from Galloway or Scotland-proper. The predominance of Gaelic began to decline in the 13th century, and by the end of the Middle Ages, Scotland was divided into two linguistic zones, the English/Scots-speaking Lowlands and the Gaelic-speaking Highlands and Galloway. Gaelic continued to be spoken widely throughout the Highlands until the 19th century. The <a href="/wiki/Highland_clearances" class="mw-redirect" title="Highland clearances">Highland clearances</a> actively discouraged the use of Gaelic, caused the numbers of Gaelic speakers to fall.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Many Gaelic speakers emigrated to countries such as Canada or moved to the industrial cities of <a href="/wiki/Lowland_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Lowland Scotland">lowland Scotland</a>. Communities where the language is still spoken natively are restricted to the west coast of Scotland; and especially the <a href="/wiki/Hebrides" title="Hebrides">Hebrides</a>. However, large proportions of Gaelic speakers also live in the cities of <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> in Scotland. A report in 2005 by the Registrar General for Scotland based on the <a href="/wiki/2001_UK_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="2001 UK Census">2001 UK Census</a> showed about 92,400 people or 1.9% of the population can speak Gaelic while the number of people able to read and write rose by 7.5% and 10% respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Outwith Scotland, there are communities of Scottish Gaelic speakers such as the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Gaelic" title="Canadian Gaelic">Canadian Gaelic</a> community; though their numbers have also been declining rapidly. Gaelic language is recognised as a minority Language by the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Scottish_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish parliament">Scottish parliament</a> is also seeking to increase the use of Gaelic in Scotland through the <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_Language_(Scotland)_Act_2005" title="Gaelic Language (Scotland) Act 2005">Gaelic Language (Scotland) Act 2005</a>. Gaelic is now used as a first language in some schools and is prominently seen in use on <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_road_signs_in_Scotland" title="Gaelic road signs in Scotland">dual language road signs</a> throughout the Gaelic speaking parts of Scotland. It is recognised as an official language of Scotland with "equal respect" to English.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Scotland" title="Religion in Scotland">Religion in Scotland</a></div>\n<p>The modern people of Scotland remain a mix of different religions and no religion. <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is the largest faith in Scotland. In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2011">2011 census</a>, 53.8% of the Scottish population identified as <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2011census_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011census-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The Protestant and Catholic divisions still remain in the society. In Scotland the main Protestant body is the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a> which is Presbyterian. The high kirk for Presbyterians is <a href="/wiki/St_Giles%27_Cathedral" title="St Giles&#39; Cathedral">St Giles\' Cathedral</a>. In the United States, people of Scottish and Scots-Irish descent are chiefly Protestant<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>, with many belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Baptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Baptist">Baptist</a> or <a href="/wiki/Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist">Methodist</a> churches, or various <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterian">Presbyterian</a> denominations.\n</p><p>According to the Social Scottish Attitudes research, 52% of Scottish people identified as having no religion in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> As a result, Scotland has thus become a secular and majority non-religious country, unique to the other UK countries.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_literature" title="Scottish literature">Scottish literature</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Folklore">Folklore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Folklore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_folklore" title="Scottish folklore">Scottish folklore</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_engineering">Science and engineering</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Science and engineering">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Scottish_scientists" title="List of Scottish scientists">List of Scottish scientists</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Synthetic_Production_of_Penicillin_TR1468_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Synthetic_Production_of_Penicillin_TR1468_crop.jpg/140px-Synthetic_Production_of_Penicillin_TR1468_crop.jpg" width="140" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Synthetic_Production_of_Penicillin_TR1468_crop.jpg/210px-Synthetic_Production_of_Penicillin_TR1468_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Synthetic_Production_of_Penicillin_TR1468_crop.jpg/280px-Synthetic_Production_of_Penicillin_TR1468_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="407" data-file-height="590" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Synthetic_Production_of_Penicillin_TR1468_crop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Alexander_Fleming" title="Alexander Fleming">Alexander Fleming</a>. His discovery of <a href="/wiki/Penicillin" title="Penicillin">penicillin</a> had changed the world of modern medicine by introducing the age of <a href="/wiki/Antibiotics" class="mw-redirect" title="Antibiotics">antibiotics</a>.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Scotland" title="Music of Scotland">Music of Scotland</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Scotland" title="Sport in Scotland">Sport in Scotland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Massed_bands.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Massed_bands.jpg/220px-Massed_bands.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Massed_bands.jpg/330px-Massed_bands.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Massed_bands.jpg/440px-Massed_bands.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Massed_bands.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Massed pipebands at the <a href="/wiki/Glengarry_Highland_Games" title="Glengarry Highland Games">Glengarry Highland Games</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, Canada</div></div></div>\n<p>The modern games of <a href="/wiki/Curling" title="Curling">curling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a> originated in Scotland. Both sports are governed by bodies headquartered in Scotland, the <a href="/wiki/World_Curling_Federation" title="World Curling Federation">World Curling Federation</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Royal_and_Ancient_Golf_Club_of_St_Andrews" title="The Royal and Ancient Golf Club of St Andrews">the Royal and Ancient Golf Club of St Andrews</a> respectively.  Scots helped to popularise and spread the sport of <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a>; the first official international match was played in Glasgow between <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> in <a href="/wiki/England_v_Scotland_(1872)" class="mw-redirect" title="England v Scotland (1872)">1872</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_cuisine" title="Scottish cuisine">Scottish cuisine</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clans">Clans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Clans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_clan" title="Scottish clan">Scottish clan</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Tartan" title="Tartan">Tartan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kilt" title="Kilt">Kilt</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scottish_clan_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Scottish_clan_map.png/220px-Scottish_clan_map.png" width="220" height="289" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Scottish_clan_map.png/330px-Scottish_clan_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Scottish_clan_map.png/440px-Scottish_clan_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1065" data-file-height="1400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scottish_clan_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Scottish highland <a href="/wiki/Scottish_clan" title="Scottish clan">clans</a> and lowland families.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mcicamp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d8/Mcicamp.jpg/170px-Mcicamp.jpg" width="170" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d8/Mcicamp.jpg/255px-Mcicamp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d8/Mcicamp.jpg/340px-Mcicamp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="466" data-file-height="650" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mcicamp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Campbell of Argyle. A <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">romanticised</a> <a href="/wiki/Victorian-era" class="mw-redirect" title="Victorian-era">Victorian-era</a> illustration of a Clansman by <a href="/wiki/R._R._McIan" title="R. R. McIan">R. R. McIan</a> from <i>The Clans of the Scottish Highlands</i> published in 1845.</div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Anglicisation">Anglicisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Anglicisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Anglicisation" title="Anglicisation">Anglicisation</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Original_research" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="40" data-file-height="40" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section  <b>possibly contains <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research">original research</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit">improve it</a> by <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verifying</a> the claims made and adding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Inline_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">inline citations</a>. Statements consisting only of original research should be removed.</span>  <small><i>(June 2010)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Many <a href="/wiki/Scottish_surnames" title="Scottish surnames">Scottish surnames</a> have become <a href="/wiki/Anglicised" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglicised">anglicised</a> over the centuries. This reflected the gradual spread of English, also known as <a href="/wiki/Early_Scots" title="Early Scots">Early Scots</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> from around the 13th century onwards, through Scotland beyond its traditional area in the Lothians. It also reflected some deliberate political attempts<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> to promote the English language in the outlying regions of Scotland, including following the Union of the Crowns under King <a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">James VI of Scotland and I of England</a> in 1603, and then the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_of_1707" class="mw-redirect" title="Acts of Union of 1707">Acts of Union of 1707</a> and the subsequent defeat of rebellions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (December 2016)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>However, many Scottish surnames have remained predominantly <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Gaelic language">Gaelic</a> albeit written according to English <a href="/wiki/Orthography" title="Orthography">orthographic</a> practice (as with Irish surnames). Thus <i>MacAoidh</i> in Gaelic is <i>Mackay</i> in English, and <i>MacGill-Eain</i> in Gaelic is <i>MacLean</i> and so on. <i>Mac</i> (sometimes <i>Mc</i>) is common as, effectively, it means "son of". <i>MacDonald</i>, <i>MacAulay</i>, <i>Gilmore</i>, <i>Gilmour</i>, <i>MacKinley</i>, <i>Macintosh</i>, <i>MacKenzie</i>, <i>MacNeill</i>, <i>MacPherson</i>, <i>MacLear</i>, <i>MacAra</i>, <i>Craig</i>, <i>Lauder</i>, <i>Menzies</i>, <i>Galloway</i> and <i>Duncan</i> are just a few of many examples of traditional Scottish surnames. There are, of course, also the many surnames, like <i>Wallace</i> and <i>Morton</i>, stemming from parts of Scotland which were settled by peoples other than the <a href="/wiki/Scoti" title="Scoti">(Gaelic) Scots</a>. The most common surnames in Scotland are <i>Smith</i> and <i>Brown</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> which come from several origins each \xe2\x80\x93 e.g. Smith can be a translation of Mac a\' Ghobhainn (thence also e.g. MacGowan), and Brown can refer to the colour, or be akin to MacBrayne.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Anglicisation is not restricted to language. In his <i>Socialism: critical and constructive</i>, published in 1921, future British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ramsay_MacDonald" title="Ramsay MacDonald">Ramsay MacDonald</a> wrote: "The Anglification of Scotland has been proceeding apace to the damage of its education, its music, its literature, its genius, and the generation that is growing up under this influence is uprooted from its past, and, being\ndeprived of the inspiration of its nationality, is also deprived of its communal sense."<sup id="cite_ref-MacDonald1921_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacDonald1921-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Scotia" title="Scotia">Scotia</a></div>\n<p>Originally the Romans used Scotia to refer to the Gaels living in Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-Lehane1994_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lehane1994-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (December 2016)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/Bede" title="Bede">The Venerable Bede</a> (c. 672 or 673 \xe2\x80\x93 27 May, 735) uses the word <i>Scottorum</i> for the nation from Ireland who settled part of the <a href="/wiki/Pictish" class="mw-redirect" title="Pictish">Pictish</a> lands: "<i>Scottorum nationem in Pictorum parte recipit</i>."  This we can infer to mean the arrival of the people, also known as the <a href="/wiki/Gaels" title="Gaels">Gaels</a>, in the Kingdom of D\xc3\xa1l Riata, in the western edge of Scotland. It is of note that Bede used the word <i>natio</i> (nation) for the Scots, where he often refers to other peoples, such as the Picts, with the word <i>gens</i> (race).<sup id="cite_ref-Harris_72_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harris_72-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> In the 10th-century <i><a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_Chronicle" title="Anglo-Saxon Chronicle">Anglo-Saxon Chronicle</a></i>, the word <i>Scot</i> is mentioned as a reference to the "Land of the Gaels". The word <i>Scottorum</i> was again used by an Irish king in 1005: <i>Imperator Scottorum</i> was the title given to <a href="/wiki/Brian_Boru" title="Brian Boru">Brian B\xc3\xb3ruma</a> by his notary, Mael Suthain, in the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Armagh" title="Book of Armagh">Book of Armagh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MoodyCr\xc3\xb3in\xc3\xadn2005_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoodyCr\xc3\xb3in\xc3\xadn2005-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> This style was subsequently copied by the Scottish kings. <i><a href="/wiki/Basileus" title="Basileus">Basileus</a> Scottorum</i> appears on the great seal of <a href="/wiki/Edgar_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Edgar of Scotland">King Edgar</a> (1074\xe2\x80\x931107).<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Scotland" title="Alexander I of Scotland">Alexander I</a> (c. 1078\xe2\x80\x931124) used the words <i><a href="/wiki/King" title="King">Rex</a> Scottorum</i> on his great seal, as did many of his successors up to and including <a href="/wiki/James_VI_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="James VI of Scotland">James VI</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PrydeGreenway1996_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PrydeGreenway1996-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In modern times the words <i>Scot</i> and <i>Scottish</i> are applied mainly to inhabitants of Scotland. The possible ancient Irish connotations are largely forgotten. The language known as <i><a href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots_dialects" title="Ulster Scots dialects">Ulster Scots</a></i>, spoken in parts of northeastern Ireland, is the result of 17th- and 18th-century immigration to Ireland from Scotland.\n</p><p>In the English language, the word <i><a href="/wiki/Scotch_(adjective)" title="Scotch (adjective)">Scotch</a></i> is a term to describe a thing from Scotland, such as <i>Scotch whisky</i>. However, when referring to people, the preferred term is <i>Scots</i>. Many Scottish people find the term <i>Scotch</i> to be offensive when applied to people.<sup id="cite_ref-Scotch_Off_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotch_Off-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The Oxford Dictionary describes <i>Scotch</i> as an old-fashioned term for "Scottish".<sup id="cite_ref-OED_Scotch_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OED_Scotch-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scottish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 15em; -webkit-column-width: 15em; column-width: 15em;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Anglo-M%C3%A9tis" title="Anglo-M\xc3\xa9tis">Anglo-Metis people</a></li>\n<li><a href="https://web.archive.org/web/20131221102601/http://www.scottishaffairs.org/onlinepub/sa/mccrone_1997-98polls.html">"Scottish Affairs, No. 24, Summer 1998; Opinion Polls in Scotland: July 1997 \xe2\x80\x93 June 1998"</a>. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.scottishaffairs.org/onlinepub/sa/mccrone_1997-98polls.html">the original</a> on 21 December 2013.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Scottish+Affairs%2C+No.+24%2C+Summer+1998%3B+Opinion+Polls+in+Scotland%3A+July+1997+%E2%80%93+June+1998&amp;rft.au=David+McCrone%2C+Professor+of+Sociology%2C+University+of+Edinburgh&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.scottishaffairs.org%2Fonlinepub%2Fsa%2Fmccrone_1997-98polls.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScottish+people" class="Z3988"></span><span class="citation-comment" style="display:none; color:#33aa33; margin-left:0.3em">CS1 maint: Multiple names: authors list (<a href="/wiki/Category:CS1_maint:_Multiple_names:_authors_list" title="Category:CS1 maint: Multiple names: authors list">link</a>) </span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/> During 1997\xe2\x80\x931998 two polls were undertaken. During the first when asked about their national identity 59 percent of the people polled stated they were Scottish or more Scottish than British, 28 percent stated they were equally Scottish and British, while 10 percent stated they were British or more British than Scottish. In the second poll 59 percent of the people polled stated they were Scottish or more Scottish than British, 26 percent stated they were equally Scottish and British, while 12 percent stated they were British or more British than Scottish.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-35">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">The Scottish Government. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.scotland.gov.uk/Publications/2006/09/14141401/4">"One Scotland Many Cultures 2005/06 \xe2\x80\x93 Waves 6 and 7 Campaign Evaluation"</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=One+Scotland+Many+Cultures+2005%2F06+%E2%80%93+Waves+6+and+7+Campaign+Evaluation&amp;rft.au=The+Scottish+Government&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.scotland.gov.uk%2FPublications%2F2006%2F09%2F14141401%2F4&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AScottish+people" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/>When asked what ethnic group they belonged over five surveys, in the 2005/2006 period, people reporting that they were Scottish rose from 75 percent to 84 percent, while those reporting that they were British dropped from 39 percent to 22 percent. "a number of respondents selected more than one option, usually both Scottish and British, hence percentages adding to more than 100% ... This indicates a continued erosion of perceived Britishness among respondents..."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Ref_y-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Ref_y_36-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://factfinder.census.gov/faces/tableservices/jsf/pages/productview.xhtml?pid=ACS_10_1YR_B04003&amp;prodType=table">"QT-P13.
